     594                 :            : /*
     595                 :            :  * prepare_for_client_read -- set up to possibly block on client input
     596                 :            :  *
     597                 :            :  * This must be called immediately before any low-level read from the
     598                 :            :  * client connection.  It is necessary to do it at a sufficiently low level
     599                 :            :  * that there won't be any other operations except the read kernel call
     600                 :            :  * itself between this call and the subsequent client_read_ended() call.
     601                 :            :  * In particular there mustn't be use of malloc() or other potentially
     602                 :            :  * non-reentrant libc functions.  This restriction makes it safe for us
     603                 :            :  * to allow interrupt service routines to execute nontrivial code while
     604                 :            :  * we are waiting for input.
     605                 :            :  *
     606                 :            :  * When waiting in the main loop, we can process any interrupt immediately
     607                 :            :  * in the signal handler. In any other read from the client, like in a COPY
     608                 :            :  * FROM STDIN, we can't safely process a query cancel signal, because we might
     609                 :            :  * be in the middle of sending a message to the client, and jumping out would
     610                 :            :  * violate the protocol. Or rather, pqcomm.c would detect it and refuse to
     611                 :            :  * send any more messages to the client. But handling a SIGTERM is OK, because
     612                 :            :  * we're terminating the backend and don't need to send any more messages
     613                 :            :  * anyway. That means that we might not be able to send an error message to
     614                 :            :  * the client, but that seems better than waiting indefinitely, in case the
     615                 :            :  * client is not responding.
     616                 :            :  */
